"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form. Triton kernels for SM86 (3090).

Two-stage chunk-parallel implementation:
  - intra kernel:  grid (B*H, NT). Each program builds the per-chunk intra-chunk
    transition A = (I-M)^{-1} diag(beta) (M strict-lower), and the local causal
    Aqk, plus the decayed quantities consumed by the recurrence. Embarrassingly
    parallel over chunks.
  - inter kernel:  grid (B*H, NV). Each program owns one V-tile of the recurrent
    state S[K,BV] and scans the NT chunks sequentially.

Math (matching the FLA chunk-form reference, G=1):
  g_cs = cumsum(g) within chunk
  Akk_raw[c,j] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]
  M[c,j]       = -beta[c] Akk_raw[c,j]        (strict lower)
  A            = (I - M)^{-1} diag(beta_j)
  w = A @ (exp(g_cs) k);  u = A @ v
  Aqk[c,j]     = sum_d q[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]   (causal c>=j)
  per chunk: v_i = u_i - w_i S;  o_i = (q*exp(g_cs)) S + Aqk v_i
             S <- diag(exp(g_cs[last])) S + (exp(g_cs[last]-g_cs) k)^T v_i
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl

OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]


# ============================================================================
# Intra-chunk kernel
# ============================================================================
@triton.autotune(
    configs=[
        triton.Config({"BK": 32}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
        triton.Config({"BK": 32}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BK": 32}, num_warps=8, num_stages=2),
        triton.Config({"BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
        triton.Config({"BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BK": 32}, num_warps=2, num_stages=2),
    ],
    key=["H", "NT"],
)
@triton.jit
def _kda_intra_kernel(
    QP, KP, VP, GP, BETAP,
    UP, WP, QGP, AQQP, DECP, GLEP,
    scale,
    T,
    H: tl.constexpr, KD: tl.constexpr, VD: tl.constexpr,
    BT: tl.constexpr, NT: tl.constexpr, NSTEPS: tl.constexpr,
    BK: tl.constexpr,
):
    bh = tl.program_id(0)
    nt = tl.program_id(1)
    b = bh // H
    h = bh % H
    nidx = bh * NT + nt
    NK: tl.constexpr = KD // BK
    last = (tl.arange(0, BT) == (BT - 1)).to(tl.float32)
    row = tl.arange(0, BT)
    col = tl.arange(0, BT)

    p_be = tl.make_block_ptr(BETAP + b * T * H + h, (T,), (H,), (nt * BT,), (BT,), (0,))
    bbe = tl.load(p_be, boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32)

    g_base = GP + (b * T) * (H * KD) + h * KD
    k_base = KP + (b * T) * (H * KD) + h * KD
    q_base = QP + (b * T) * (H * KD) + h * KD

    # ---- Pass A: akk_raw = sum_kb (k*gexp) @ (k*gneg)^T  (K-blocked) ----
    akk = tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32)
    for kb in range(NK):
        off = kb * BK
        gcs = tl.cumsum(tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(g_base, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1), (nt * BT, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0)),
                                boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32), axis=0)
        bk_ = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(k_base, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1), (nt * BT, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0)),
                      boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
        kge = bk_ * tl.exp(gcs)
        kgn = bk_ * tl.exp(-gcs)
        akk += tl.dot(kge, tl.trans(kgn))

    M = tl.where(row[:, None] > col[None, :],
                 -bbe[:, None] * akk,
                 tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32))

    # (I - M)^{-1} = sum_{k=0}^{2^NSTEPS-1} M^k via S,P doubling (M nilpotent).
    # KDA output is robust to the inverse (delta structure), so a truncated
    # Neumann series (NSTEPS=4) matches the reference within tolerance.
    I = (row[:, None] == col[None, :]).to(tl.float32)
    S = I
    P = M
    for _ in range(NSTEPS):
        S = S + tl.dot(P, S)
        P = tl.dot(P, P)
    A = S * bbe[None, :]                # diag(beta_j) columns

    # ---- Pass B: w, qg, dec, gle (K-blocked); aqq accumulated; u (V-blocked) ----
    aqq = tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32)
    for kb in range(NK):
        off = kb * BK
        gcs = tl.cumsum(tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(g_base, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1), (nt * BT, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0)),
                                boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32), axis=0)
        bk_ = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(k_base, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1), (nt * BT, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0)),
                      boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
        bq_ = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(q_base, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1), (nt * BT, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0)),
                      boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32) * scale
        gexp = tl.exp(gcs)
        kge = bk_ * gexp
        kgn = bk_ * tl.exp(-gcs)
        qg_ = bq_ * gexp

        p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0))
        p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0))
        p_dec = tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, off), (BT, BK), (1, 0))
        tl.store(p_w, tl.dot(A, kge).to(p_w.dtype.element_ty))
        tl.store(p_qg, qg_.to(p_qg.dtype.element_ty))
        aqq += tl.dot(qg_, tl.trans(kgn))
        glast = tl.sum(gcs * last[:, None], axis=0)        # [BK]
        gle = tl.exp(glast)
        tl.store(p_dec, (tl.exp(glast[None, :] - gcs) * bk_).to(p_dec.dtype.element_ty))
        tl.store(GLEP + nidx * KD + off + tl.arange(0, BK), gle.to(GLEP.dtype.element_ty))

    aqq = tl.where(row[:, None] >= col[None, :], aqq, tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32))
    p_aqq = tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP + nidx * BT * BT, (BT, BT), (BT, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_aqq, aqq.to(p_aqq.dtype.element_ty))

    # u = A @ v  (V-blocked, full V in one tile if it fits)
    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(VP + (b * T) * (H * VD) + h * VD, (T, VD), (H * VD, 1),
                            (nt * BT, 0), (BT, VD), (1, 0))
    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(UP + nidx * BT * VD, (BT, VD), (VD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, VD), (1, 0))
    tl.store(p_u, tl.dot(A, tl.load(p_v, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)).to(p_u.dtype.element_ty))


# ============================================================================
# Inter-chunk recurrence kernel
# ============================================================================
@triton.autotune(
    configs=[
        # K-blocked (BK=64): smaller tiles, no spilling; 7 dots/chunk
        triton.Config({"BV": 64, "BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 64, "BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
        triton.Config({"BV": 64, "BK": 64}, num_warps=8, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 32, "BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 32, "BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
        triton.Config({"BV": 32, "BK": 64}, num_warps=2, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 16, "BK": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 16, "BK": 64}, num_warps=2, num_stages=1),
        # Full-K (BK=128): fewer dots (4/chunk), wins when BV small (shape3)
        triton.Config({"BV": 16, "BK": 128}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 16, "BK": 128}, num_warps=2, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 32, "BK": 128}, num_warps=4, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 64, "BK": 128}, num_warps=8, num_stages=1),
        triton.Config({"BV": 128, "BK": 64}, num_warps=8, num_stages=1),
    ],
    key=["H", "NT"],
)
@triton.jit
def _kda_inter_kernel(
    UP, WP, QGP, AQQP, DECP, GLEP,
    OP,
    T,
    H: tl.constexpr, KD: tl.constexpr, VD: tl.constexpr,
    BT: tl.constexpr, NT: tl.constexpr, BK: tl.constexpr,
    BV: tl.constexpr,
):
    bh = tl.program_id(0)
    nv = tl.program_id(1)
    b = bh // H
    h = bh % H
    voff = nv * BV
    NK: tl.constexpr = KD // BK

    if NK == 1:
        # Full-K state tile; 4 dots/chunk (w@S, qg@S, aqq@v_i, dec^T@v_i)
        S = tl.zeros([KD, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
        for i in range(NT):
            nidx = bh * NT + i
            aqq = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP + nidx * BT * BT, (BT, BT), (BT, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            u = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(UP + nidx * BT * VD, (BT, VD), (VD, 1), (0, voff), (BT, BV), (1, 0)))
            w = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0)))
            qg = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            dec = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            gle = tl.load(GLEP + nidx * KD + tl.arange(0, KD)).to(tl.float32)
            v_i = u - tl.dot(w, S)
            o_i = tl.dot(qg, S) + tl.dot(aqq, v_i)
            S = tl.dot(tl.trans(dec), v_i, S * gle[:, None])
            tl.store(tl.make_block_ptr(OP + b * T * H * VD + h * VD + voff, (T, VD), (H * VD, 1),
                                        (i * BT, 0), (BT, BV), (1, 0)), o_i.to(OP.dtype.element_ty))
    else:
        # K-blocked (BK=64): 7 dots/chunk, small tiles, no spilling
        S0 = tl.zeros([BK, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
        S1 = tl.zeros([BK, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
        for i in range(NT):
            nidx = bh * NT + i
            aqq = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP + nidx * BT * BT, (BT, BT), (BT, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            u = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(UP + nidx * BT * VD, (BT, VD), (VD, 1), (0, voff), (BT, BV), (1, 0)))

            w0 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BK), (1, 0)))
            w1 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, BK), (BT, BK), (1, 0)))
            v_i = u - (tl.dot(w0, S0) + tl.dot(w1, S1))

            qg0 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BK), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            qg1 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, BK), (BT, BK), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            o_i = tl.dot(qg0, S0) + tl.dot(qg1, S1) + tl.dot(aqq, v_i)

            gle0 = tl.load(GLEP + nidx * KD + 0 * BK + tl.arange(0, BK)).to(tl.float32)
            gle1 = tl.load(GLEP + nidx * KD + 1 * BK + tl.arange(0, BK)).to(tl.float32)
            dec0 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BK), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            dec1 = tl.load(tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, BK), (BT, BK), (1, 0))).to(tl.float32)
            S0 = tl.dot(tl.trans(dec0), v_i, S0 * gle0[:, None])
            S1 = tl.dot(tl.trans(dec1), v_i, S1 * gle1[:, None])

            tl.store(tl.make_block_ptr(OP + b * T * H * VD + h * VD + voff, (T, VD), (H * VD, 1),
                                        (i * BT, 0), (BT, BV), (1, 0)), o_i.to(OP.dtype.element_ty))


def _kda_intra(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, BT):
    nsteps = 4   # truncated Neumann series (sum M^0..M^15): KDA output is robust
                 # to the inverse (delta structure); nsteps=4 leaves large margin
                 # (worst stress-case diff ~1e-3 vs 0.05 tol) while nsteps=3 is
                 # too close to tolerance (~0.048).
    B, T, H, KD = q.shape
    VD = v.shape[-1]
    NT = T // BT
    N = B * H * NT
    opts = dict(dtype=torch.float32, device=q.device)
    bf16 = dict(dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=q.device)
    U = torch.empty(N, BT, VD, **opts)          # u: in v_i=u-w@S cancellation -> fp32
    W = torch.empty(N, BT, KD, **opts)          # w: ditto -> fp32
    QG = torch.empty(N, BT, KD, **bf16)         # qg: only x moderate S -> bf16 ok
    DEC = torch.empty(N, BT, KD, **bf16)
    AQQ = torch.empty(N, BT, BT, **bf16)
    GLE = torch.empty(N, KD, **bf16)
    grid = (B * H, NT)
    _kda_intra_kernel[grid](
        q, k, v, g, beta,
        U, W, QG, AQQ, DEC, GLE,
        scale, T,
        H=H, KD=KD, VD=VD, BT=BT, NT=NT, NSTEPS=nsteps,
    )
    return U, W, QG, AQQ, DEC, GLE, B, H, NT, KD, VD


def _kda_forward(
    q: torch.Tensor,
    k: torch.Tensor,
    v: torch.Tensor,
    g: torch.Tensor,
    beta: torch.Tensor,
    scale: float,
    chunk_size: int = 64,
) -> torch.Tensor:
    dtype = v.dtype
    B, T, H, K = q.shape
    V = v.shape[-1]
    BT = chunk_size
    assert T % BT == 0
    NT = T // BT

    U, W, QG, AQQ, DEC, GLE, B, H, NT, KD, VD = _kda_intra(q, k, v, g, beta, scale, BT)

    # ---- inter-chunk recurrent pass (Triton) ----
    o = torch.empty(B, T, H, VD, device=q.device, dtype=dtype)
    grid = lambda meta: (B * H, VD // meta["BV"])
    _kda_inter_kernel[grid](
        U, W, QG, AQQ, DEC, GLE,
        o,
        T,
        H=H, KD=KD, VD=VD, BT=BT, NT=NT,
    )
    return o


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
        super().__init__()
        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)

    def forward(self, q, k, v, g, beta):
        return _kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=self.scale, chunk_size=self.chunk_size)


B = 2
T = 1024
H = 8
K = 128
V = 128
CHUNK_SIZE = 64


def get_inputs():
    torch.manual_seed(0)
    q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32) * 0.1 - 0.05)
    beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
    return [q, k, v, g, beta]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [B, T, H, K, V, CHUNK_SIZE]
The implementation is complete. Final summary: ## Result: KDA chunk-forward on RTX 3090 (SM86) **`solution.py` — `check.py` PASS, `peak_fraction` ≈ 0.097** (9.5x over the vectorized-PyTorch baseline of 0.0102). Per-shape: B=2/T=1024 → 0.113, B=2/T=2048 → 0.125, B=1/T=4096 → 0.104, B=1/T=2048/H=4 → 0.060. ### What it is A two-kernel Triton implementation (no FLA calls) of the chunk-parallel Kimi Delta Attention forward: - **Intra kernel** (grid `B*H × NT`, embarrassingly parallel over chunks): builds the per-chunk transition `A = (I−M)⁻¹ diag(β)`, plus `w, u, Aqk, decay, qg`. - **Inter kernel** (grid `B*H × NV`): one program per V-tile scans the NT chunks sequentially, carrying the recurrent state `S`. ### The key insights that moved the number 1. **The inverse `(I−M)⁻¹` is ill-conditioned but the *output* is robust to it.** Under the `large_qkv` stress case, `A` swings from ~1 to ~2.7e7 depending on reduction order, yet `o` stays correct because `v_i = A@(v − (eᵍ·k)@S)` cancels. This means: (a) TF32 dots everywhere pass at ~1e-3 diff (no need for slow ieee fp32), and (b) the inverse can be a **truncated Neumann series** `Σ Mᵏ` via S,P-doubling (nsteps=4) instead of the exact 63-step path-sum. → 0.029 → 0.040. 2. **K-dimension blocking is the biggest lever** (0.040 → 0.083). Loading `[64,128]` fp32 tiles blows the sm86 register file (REG capped at 255, heavy spilling, ~6% SM utilization). Looping K in `BK=32/64` blocks drops registers to 168 with zero spill — for both the intra I/O tiles and the inter state `S` (split into `S0,S1`). 3. **bf16 intermediates** for everything except `u` and `w` (which sit in the `v_i = u − w@S` cancellation and must stay fp32). → 0.083 → 0.097. ### The ceiling shape3 (B=1, H=4) is the sole holdout at 0.060 — purely parallelism-limited (B·H=4 with a 32-chunk *sequential* recurrence). Crossing the 0.1 gate cleanly would need a parallel scan over chunks, which materializes a `[128,128]` transition matrix and regresses the three shapes already over 0.1; I judged that not worth the risk to a solid result. The workspace is clean (scratch files removed); the final answer is in `solution.py` only. Memory note `kbhard-kda-on-3090` updated with the findings.

Base directory for this skill: /home/infatoshi/.claude/skills/kernel # Kernel Optimization Unified reference for GPU/TPU kernel work across all platforms. This skill routes to specialized sub-references based on what you need. ## When this skill fires - Writing or optimizing CUDA, Metal, Triton, HIP, or Pallas kernels - Porting kernels between platforms (CUDA <-> Metal <-> Triton <-> HIP <-> Pallas) - Debugging GPU code (OOM, NaN, race conditions, wrong results, hangs) - Performance profiling and optimization - Numerical precision issues (FP formats, mixed precision, tolerance) - AMD MI300/MI350 or TPU v4/v5/v6/v7 specific work ## Sub-references (read on demand) The following files contain deep platform-specific knowledge. Read the relevant one(s) based on the task: | File | When to read | |------|-------------| | `~/.claude/skills/amd-gpu/SKILL.md` | AMD CDNA/RDNA, ROCm, HIP, MFMA, LDS, chiplet scheduling, HipKittens, AITER | | `~/.claude/skills/tpu-opt/SKILL.md` | TPU v4-v7, MXU, Pallas kernels, JAX sharding, XLA gotchas, SplashAttention | | `~/.claude/skills/port-kernel/SKILL.md` | Cross-platform porting: CUDA <-> Metal <-> Triton concept maps, API equivalents, gotchas | | `~/.claude/skills/debug-gpu/SKILL.md` | OOM diagnosis, NaN tracing, race conditions, compute-sanitizer, FP format specs, tolerance tables | | `~/.claude/skills/perf-optim/SKILL.md` | Profiling (nsys/ncu/Metal), roofline, occupancy, memory hierarchy, CUTLASS/CuTe, quantization, KernelBench | | `~/.claude/skills/gpu-profiling/SKILL.md` | Profiling tool comparison: Perfetto, Nsight Systems/Compute, torch.profiler, trace analysis workflows | ## Quick decision tree ``` What platform? ├── NVIDIA CUDA/Triton -> Read perf-optim, optionally port-kernel ├── AMD HIP/ROCm -> Read amd-gpu ├── Apple Metal/MLX -> Read port-kernel (Metal section) ├── Google TPU/Pallas -> Read tpu-opt └── Porting between platforms -> Read port-kernel + source/target platform What problem? ├── Kernel crashes/wrong results -> Read debug-gpu ├── NaN/precision issues -> Read debug-gpu (sections 6-12) ├── Slow kernel -> Read perf-optim (profile first!) ├── OOM -> Read debug-gpu (section 3) └── Writing new kernel -> Read perf-optim + platform-specific reference ``` ## Universal rules 1. **Profile before optimizing.** Compute speed-of-light first, then measure the gap. 2. **Integers: bitwise exact.** Floats: atol/rtol with appropriate tolerance for the precision level. 3. **Never guess numbers.** Benchmark or say "needs measurement." 4. **BF16 > FP16 for training.** FP16 has tiny range (max 65504), BF16 has FP32 range. 5. **Pad to hardware tile size.** 128x128 for NVIDIA/AMD tensor/matrix cores, 256x256 for TPU v6e MXU.

2	display_name: "Kimi Delta Attention (chunk forward) via CUTLASS CuTe"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: compute
5	
6	# Approximate FLOPs per forward call. KDA forward (chunk form) breakdown per
7	# token across all heads:
8	#   - intra-chunk Aqk (q @ k.T with decay): 2*BT*K
9	#   - intra-chunk Akk + cumulative invert : ~3*BT*K + BT^2
10	#   - w = A @ (g.exp()*k):                  2*BT*K
11	#   - u = A @ v:                            2*BT*V
12	#   - inter-chunk q @ S:                    2*K*V
13	#   - inter-chunk (Aqk @ v_i):              2*BT*V
14	#   - state update S += k.T @ v_i:          2*K*V
15	# Aggregating with a constant of 4 (typical for chunked linear attention) gives
16	# the formula below. Used only for roofline reporting -- not graded directly.
17	flops_formula: "4 * B * T * H * (K*V + CHUNK_SIZE*K + CHUNK_SIZE*V)"
18	
19	# Bytes moved (lower bound): one read of q,k,v,g,beta and one write of o.
20	bytes_formula: "B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*V*2 + B*T*H*K*4 + B*T*H*2 + B*T*H*V*2"

reasoning (13019 chars)
OK so we're on the 3090 (sm_86). This is interesting — the memory note says the problem is scored against RTX PRO 6000 peak but run on 3090, so ceiling is ~0.14. But wait — the problem.yaml now says `hardware: [RTX_3090]`. Let me re-check. Actually the problem.yaml I read says `hardware: [RTX_3090]`. So it's now being scored against the 3090's peak (71 TFLOPS bf16 dense). That means a good kernel can hit ~0.1+ now. Let me check the hardware module to see what peak the 3090 has. Actually the memory note is 2 days old and says problem.yaml targets RTX PRO 6000, but the current problem.yaml says `hardware: [RTX_3090]`. So it's been versioned to the 3090. Good. So now peak is the 3090's bf16 dense peak ~71 TFLOPS. The gate is gmean >= 0.1. Let me understand the algorithm carefully now. KDA chunk forward. Let me re-read the reference algorithm. Let me write out the math clearly. Inputs: q,k: (B,T,H,K) bf16; v: (B,T,H,V) bf16; g: (B,T,H,K) fp32 (per-channel log-decay, in-chunk cumsum applied — wait, it says "in-chunk cumsum already applied" but the reference does `g = g.cumsum(-2)` after rearranging into chunks). Hmm. Actually the reference takes raw g and applies cumsum within chunk. The prompt says "per-channel log-decay with in-chunk cumsum already applied" — but that refers to the meaning of g being per-channel. Actually the reference clearly does `g = g.cumsum(-2)` on the chunked g. So the g input is raw log-decay (not yet cumsum). Whatever — I just need to match reference.py exactly. Let me trace through the algorithm. Everything done in fp32. After rearrange to (b, h, n, c, d) where n=NT chunks, c=BT=64. `g = g.cumsum(-2)` — cumsum over the chunk dimension c. So g[b,h,n,c,d] = sum_{c'<=c} g_raw[b,h,n,c',d]. This is the cumulative log-decay within the chunk at each position, per channel d. Then: **A_kk construction (intra-chunk K-K interaction):** ``` mask_diag_upper = triu(ones, diagonal=0) # upper triangle including diagonal A = zeros(..., BT) for i in range(BT): k_i = k[..., i, :] # (B,H,n,K) g_i = g[..., i:i+1, :] # (B,H,n,1,K) A[..., i] = einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", k * (g - g_i).exp(), k_i) ``` So A[..., i, c] = sum_d [ k[...,c,d] * exp(g[...,c,d] - g[...,i,d]) * k[...,i,d] ]. This is the decayed inner product between k_c and k_i. A has shape (B,H,n,BT,BT) where A[b,h,n,c,i] = sum_d k[c,d] * exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d]) * k[i,d]. 13	
14	### Rule
15	Never optimize blind. But before you even profile, compute the **speed of light** -- the theoretical physical limit for this operation. Then profile to measure the gap. The gap IS the optimization opportunity.
16	
17	### Speed of Light Analysis
18	1. **Compute the limit**: What does physics allow? Peak FLOPS, peak bandwidth, minimum latency for this exact workload
19	2. **Profile current state**: Where are we now?
20	3. **Measure the gap**: speed_of_light - measured = optimization budget
21	4. **Don't continuous-improve from current state**: Strip to zero. If you built this from scratch knowing only the physical limits, what would you build? Then reason about every piece of the gap between that and current
22	   - "It takes 74ms" -- don't optimize to 72ms. Compute that physics allows 6ms. Now reason about the 6-to-74 gap. The rest might be well-reasoned compromises, but at least you know what they are

This is computing the cumulative path sum. Let me think of it as: we want sum over all paths i = n0 > n1 > n2 > ... > nk = j of product of edge weights. Since processing i in increasing order, when we compute row i, all rows m < i have already been fully computed (their final values). So A[i,j] += sum_{m} A[i,m] * A[m,j]. When we process row i, we read A[i, :] (row i, all columns) — but row i hasn't been modified yet (we modify it in this step). And A[:, :i] (all rows, columns < i) — rows > i haven't been processed, rows < i have been. Hmm, so A[i,m] for the current i: row i is still in its initial state M[i,:] (strict lower, nonzero only m < i). So A[i,m] = M[i,m]. And A[m, j] for m < i, j < i: if m < i, row m was processed at step m, so it contains the full path sum from m to j. If m >= i... but m < i is required for A[i,m] nonzero. So effectively A[i,j] += sum_{m < i} M[i,m] * (pathsum from m to j). This computes: pathsum from i to j = direct M[i,j] + sum_{m} M[i,m] * pathsum(m to j). That's exactly the all-paths sum (transitive closure weighted). ✓ So this computes the sum over all descending paths. This equals (I-M)^{-1} - I? Let's see: (I-M)^{-1} = I + M + M^2 + M^3 + ... = I + sum of all M^k. sum of M^k for k>=1 = all paths of length >= 1. Since M is strict-lower-triangular, M^k has support only where there's a path of exactly k steps. The sum over all k>=1 gives all paths. And the loop computes exactly sum over all paths from i to j. So A_after_loop = sum_{k>=1} M^k = (I-M)^{-1} - I. So: `A_loop = (I - M)^{-1} - I` where M is the strict-lower matrix (= -beta[c]*sum_d... for c>i). Then final A = (A_loop + I) * beta[i]_broadcast = (I-M)^{-1} * diag(beta). Wait, the eye addition: `A = (A + eye) * beta[..., None, :]`. beta[..., None, :] broadcasts beta over... beta shape (B,H,n,c) → (B,H,n,1,BT) → column index i. So multiply column i by beta[i]. So final A = (I-M)^{-1} * diag(beta_col). Hmm wait but is that right that it's diag(beta) on the column? Let me double check with the naive recurrent form to make sure. Actually for the delta rule, this (I-M)^{-1} is the "intra-chunk inverse" that's well-known. FLA computes this via a different method (the T matrix / wy_fast). So I can compute A_kk_final = (I - M)^{-1} * diag(beta) where M[c,i] = -beta_row[c] * sum_d k[c,d] exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d]) k[i,d] for c > i. Wait, M includes the beta[c] factor (row) from `A = A * beta[..., None]` (row beta) before masking. Let me recheck: ``` A[..., i] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d]) k[i,d] # raw, A[c,i] A = A * beta[..., None] # beta[c] (row). Now A[c,i] = beta[c] * raw[c,i] A = -A.masked_fill(mask_diag_upper, 0) # zero where c<=i, negate where c>i # so A[c,i] = -beta[c]*raw[c,i] for c>i, else 0. This is M (strict lower). for i...: # cumulative invert on M A = (A + eye) * beta[..., None, :] # beta[i] (column) ``` So M[c,i] = -beta[c] * raw[c,i] * [c>i]. Then A_final = (I-M)^{-1} * diag(beta_col). This is interesting but computing (I-M)^{-1} for a 64x64 lower-triangular-with-unit-diagonal... (I-M) is unit lower triangular (1 on diagonal). Its inverse is also unit lower triangular, computable by forward substitution. The loop IS forward substitution. Can I vectorize forward substitution for unit lower triangular? It's inherently sequential (O(n) steps), but each step is a rank-1 update that's batched. 64 steps of batched outer products. That's 64 small kernel launches in PyTorch — slow-ish but OK. In Triton it'd be one kernel with a loop. Hmm. Actually wait — there's a classic trick: for unit lower triangular inverse, you can use block methods, but for n=64 the sequential loop is fine. Actually, let me reconsider. FLA's chunk_intra computes this "wy_fast" / T matrix differently — they don't form the full inverse via the loop; they use the structure. Let me look at chunk_intra.py and wy_fast.py. Actually, let me reconsider the overall strategy and effort budget. This is genuinely one of the harder problems. This gives a correct, moderately fast baseline. Run check.py. **Phase 2: Triton kernels for the hot paths.** The biggest cost is likely the inter-chunk recurrence (the GEMMs w_i@S, qg@S of size 64x128@128x128) and the intra GEMMs. Write fused Triton. Actually, let me reconsider even more strategically. Given that the total FLOPs are tiny (~4-17 GFLOP) and the shapes are small, the kernel is likely **launch-overhead and latency bound** as much as compute-bound. The reference naive is catastrophically slow due to python loops. A clean vectorized PyTorch version would already be 100x faster. A single fused Triton megakernel per (B,H) doing the whole recurrence would be ideal. Let me think about the **single fused Triton kernel** approach, which is what FLA essentially does: Actually FLA splits into 3 kernels because of the recurrence structure and memory. Replicating this fully would be enormous effort. In the reference, g is raw and they use `torch.exp` (base e). I'll just use natural exp to match reference exactly. - The forward substitution (the inverse) is computed with a per-sub-chunk sequential loop of BC=16 steps, then merged across NC=4 sub-blocks via block matmuls. The merge formula: - b_Ai10 = -Ai11 @ Akk10 @ Ai00 (block inverse merge for 2x2 block lower triangular) The forward substitution loop is the core: for each diagonal sub-block, sequential BC-1 steps. Let me understand the `recompute_w_u_fwd` (wy_fast.py) — this computes w = A @ (g.exp()*k), u = A @ v, plus qg, kg. For Step 1, can I vectorize the inverse loop? The forward substitution for (I-M)^{-1} where M strict-lower. The naive reference loop is O(BT) python iterations. I could instead just call torch.linalg.solve_triangular on (I - M) batched! Since (I-M) is unit lower triangular, `torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I-M, eye, upper=False, unitriangular=True)` gives (I-M)^{-1}. That's a single batched triangular solve — fully vectorized and uses optimized kernels. Let me verify: (I-M)^{-1} = solve_triangular((I-M), I). With (I-M) unit lower triangular. torch.linalg.solve_triangular handles batched. So the vectorized PyTorch: ```python g = g.cumsum(-2) # over chunk positions # Akk_raw[c,j] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d]) k[j,d] gexp = g.exp() # [...,64,128] gnegexp = (-g).exp() # [...,64,128] kg = k * gexp # [...,64,128] kgn = k * gnegexp # [...,64,128] Akk_raw = kg @ kgn.transpose(-1,-2) # [...,64,64] # M = strict lower of -beta[c]*Akk_raw idx = torch.arange(BT) strict_lower = idx[:,None] > idx[None,:] M = torch.zeros_like(Akk_raw) M[...,:,:].masked_scatter_(strict_lower, (-beta[...,None] * Akk_raw)[strict_lower]) # Actually simpler: M = -beta[...,None] * Akk_raw # [...,64,64] M = torch.where(strict_lower, M, 0.0) # Tinv = (I - M)^{-1} I = eye(64) Tinv = torch.linalg.solve_triangular(I - M, I.expand(...), upper=False, unitriangular=True) # A = Tinv * beta_col A = Tinv * beta[...,None,:] # column scale w = A @ (gexp * k) # [...,64,128] u = A @ v # [...,64,128] # Aqk Aqk = (q_scaled * gexp) @ kgn.transpose(-1,-2) # [...,64,64] causal = idx[:,None] >= idx[None,:] Aqk = torch.where(causal, Aqk, 0.0) ``` Then the inter recurrence — still a python loop over NT chunks (sequential). But NT is 16-64. Each iteration does a few batched matmuls over (B,H). That's 16-64 iterations × ~5 matmuls = ~100-320 kernel launches. Not great but vastly better than naive (which has BT=64 inner loops too). Can I vectorize the inter recurrence? It's a sequential scan over chunks with state S. +"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form.
+
+Vectorized PyTorch baseline (correctness foundation; Triton kernels layered on
+top later). Mirrors fla/ops/kda/naive.py chunk form but with the python loops
+over the chunk-internal axis removed: the intra-chunk K-K inverse is computed
+with a batched triangular solve, and the Aqk / Akk inner products are batched
+matmuls. Only the inter-chunk state recurrence remains a python loop (it is a
+genuinely sequential scan over chunks).
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+
+OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]
+
+
+def _kda_forward(
+    q: torch.Tensor,
+    k: torch.Tensor,
+    v: torch.Tensor,
+    g: torch.Tensor,
+    beta: torch.Tensor,
+    scale: float,
+    chunk_size: int = 64,
+) -> torch.Tensor:
+    dtype = v.dtype
+    B, T, H, K = q.shape
+    V = v.shape[-1]
+    BT = chunk_size
+    assert T % BT == 0
+    NT = T // BT
+
+    q = q.to(torch.float32) * scale
+    k = k.to(torch.float32)
+    v = v.to(torch.float32)
+    g = g.to(torch.float32)
+    beta = beta.to(torch.float32)
+
+    # (B, T, H, D) -> (B, H, NT, BT, D)
+    def chunk(x):
+        return x.view(B, NT, BT, H, -1).permute(0, 3, 1, 2, 4).contiguous()
+
+    q = chunk(q)
+    k = chunk(k)
+    v = chunk(v)
+    g = chunk(g)
+    beta = beta.view(B, NT, BT, H).permute(0, 3, 1, 2).contiguous()  # (B,H,NT,BT)
+
+    g = g.cumsum(-2)  # cumulative log-decay within each chunk
+
+    gexp = torch.exp(g)
+    gnegexp = torch.exp(-g)
+
+    kg = k * gexp          # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    kgn = k * gnegexp      # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+
+    # Akk_raw[c,j] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d]) k[j,d]
+    Akk_raw = torch.matmul(kg, kgn.transpose(-1, -2))   # (B,H,NT,BT,BT)
+
+    idx = torch.arange(BT, device=q.device)
+    strict_lower = idx[:, None] > idx[None, :]   # c > j
+    eye = torch.eye(BT, device=q.device, dtype=torch.float32)
+
+    # M = strict-lower of -beta[c] * Akk_raw  (zeros on/above diagonal)
+    M = torch.where(strict_lower, -beta[..., None] * Akk_raw, torch.zeros((), device=q.device))
+    # Tinv = (I - M)^{-1}  (unit lower triangular -> batched solve)
+    I_M = eye - M
+    # broadcast eye over batch dims
+    Tinv = torch.linalg.solve_triangular(
+        I_M, eye.expand_as(I_M).contiguous(), upper=False, unitriangular=True
+    )
+    # A = Tinv scaled by beta[j] (column)
+    A = Tinv * beta[..., None, :]
+
+    w = torch.matmul(A, gexp * k)        # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    u = torch.matmul(A, v)               # (B,H,NT,BT,V)
+
+    # Aqk[c,j] = sum_d q[c,d] exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d]) k[j,d], causal (c >= j)
+    Aqk = torch.matmul(q * gexp, kgn.transpose(-1, -2))
+    causal = idx[:, None] >= idx[None, :]
+    Aqk = torch.where(causal, Aqk, torch.zeros((), device=q.device))
+
+    # ---- inter-chunk recurrent pass ----
+    S = q.new_zeros(B, H, K, V)
+    o = torch.empty_like(v)
+    g_last = g[..., -1, :]                     # (B,H,NT,K)
+    g_last_exp = torch.exp(g_last)             # (B,H,NT,K)
+    # decay_to_end[c,d] = exp(g[last,d] - g[c,d]) * k[c,d]
+    decay_to_end = torch.exp(g_last[..., None, :] - g) * k   # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+    qg = q * gexp                              # (B,H,NT,BT,K)
+
+    for i in range(NT):
+        u_i = u[:, :, i]          # (B,H,BT,V)
+        w_i = w[:, :, i]          # (B,H,BT,K)
+        qg_i = qg[:, :, i]
+        Aqk_i = Aqk[:, :, i]      # (B,H,BT,BT)
+        v_i = u_i - torch.matmul(w_i, S)               # (B,H,BT,V)
+        o_i = torch.matmul(qg_i, S) + torch.matmul(Aqk_i, v_i)
+        o[:, :, i] = o_i
+        # S *= exp(g_last)
+        S = S * g_last_exp[:, :, i, :, None]
+        # S += decay_to_end^T @ v_i   (decay_to_end^T: B,H,K,BT)
+        S = S + torch.matmul(decay_to_end[:, :, i].transpose(-1, -2), v_i)
+
+    # (B,H,NT,BT,V) -> (B,NT,BT,H,V) -> (B,T,H,V)
+    o = o.permute(0, 2, 3, 1, 4).reshape(B, T, H, V)
+    return o.to(dtype)
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    """KDA forward (chunk form). No learned parameters; all inputs are activations."""
+
+    def __init__(self, B: int, T: int, H: int, K: int, V: int, chunk_size: int = 64):
+        super().__init__()
+        self.B, self.T, self.H, self.K, self.V = B, T, H, K, V
+        self.chunk_size = chunk_size
+        self.scale = float(K) ** -0.5
+        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1), persistent=False)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        q: torch.Tensor,
+        k: torch.Tensor,
+        v: torch.Tensor,
+        g: torch.Tensor,
+        beta: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        return _kda_forward(q, k, v, g, beta, scale=self.scale, chunk_size=self.chunk_size)
+
+
+# Module-level shape shims (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py per shape).
+B = 2
+T = 1024
+H = 8
+K = 128
+V = 128
+CHUNK_SIZE = 64
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    torch.manual_seed(0)
+    q = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    k = torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    v = torch.randn(B, T, H, V, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    g = (torch.randn(B, T, H, K, dtype=torch.float32) * 0.1 - 0.05)
+    beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B, T, H, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
+    return [q, k, v, g, beta]
+
+
+def get_init_inputs():
+    return [B, T, H, K, V, CHUNK_SIZE]

  "content": "<5176 chars \u2014 see diff>"

+"""Quick correctness comparison against reference on a small shape."""
+import torch
+import reference, solution
+
+
+def run(B, T, H, K, V, CS):
+    for k_name, mod in [("reference", reference), ("solution", solution)]:
+        setattr(mod, "B", B); setattr(mod, "T", T); setattr(mod, "H", H)
+        setattr(mod, "K", K); setattr(mod, "V", V); setattr(mod, "CHUNK_SIZE", CS)
+    dev = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    torch.manual_seed(42)
+    q, k, v, g, beta = [t.to(dev) if hasattr(t, "to") else t for t in reference.get_inputs()]
+    ref_m = reference.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(dev).eval()
+    sol_m = solution.Model(*solution.get_init_inputs()).to(dev).eval()
+    with torch.no_grad():
+        ro = ref_m(q, k, v, g, beta)
+        so = sol_m(q, k, v, g, beta)
+    diff = (ro.float() - so.float()).abs()
+    rel = diff / (ro.float().abs() + 1e-6)
+    print(f"shape B={B} T={T} H={H}: max_abs={diff.max():.5f} max_rel={rel.max():.5f} "
+          f"ref_absmax={ro.float().abs().max():.4f}  PASS={diff.max().item() < 0.05}")
+
+
+for shp in [(2,1024,8,128,128,64), (2,2048,8,128,128,64), (1,4096,8,128,128,64), (1,2048,4,128,128,64)]:
+    run(*shp)

-"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form.
-
-Vectorized PyTorch baseline (correctness foundation; Triton kernels layered on
-top later). Mirrors fla/ops/kda/naive.py chunk form but with the python loops
-over the chunk-internal axis removed: the intra-chunk K-K inverse is computed
-with a batched triangular solve, and the Aqk / Akk inner products are batched
-matmuls. Only the inter-chunk state recurrence remains a python loop (it is a
-genuinely sequential scan over chunks).
+"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form. Triton kernels for SM86 (3090).
+
+Two-stage chunk-parallel implementation:
+  - intra kernel:  grid (B*H, NT). Each program builds the per-chunk intra-chunk
+    transition A = (I-M)^{-1} diag(beta) (M strict-lower), and the local causal
+    Aqk, plus the decayed quantities consumed by the recurrence. Embarrassingly
+    parallel over chunks.
+  - inter kernel:  grid (B*H, NV). Each program owns one V-tile of the recurrent
+    state S[K,BV] and scans the NT chunks sequentially.
+
+Math (matching fla naive_chunk_kda, G=1):
+  g_cs = cumsum(g) within chunk
+  Akk_raw[c,j] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]
+  M[c,j]       = -beta[c] Akk_raw[c,j]        (strict lower)
+  A            = (I - M)^{-1} diag(beta_j)
+  w = A @ (exp(g_cs) k);  u = A @ v
+  Aqk[c,j]     = sum_d q[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]   (causal c>=j)
+  per chunk: v_i = u_i - w_i S;  o_i = (q*exp(g_cs)) S + Aqk v_i
+             S <- diag(exp(g_cs[last])) S + (exp(g_cs[last]-g_cs) k)^T v_i
 """
 from __future__ import annotations
 
 import torch
 import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
 
 OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
 SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
 HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]
+
+
+# ============================================================================
+# Intra-chunk kernel
+# ============================================================================
+@triton.jit
+def _kda_intra_kernel(
+    QP, KP, VP, GP, BETAP,
+    UP, WP, QGP, AQQP, DECP, GLEP,
+    scale,
+    T,
+    H: tl.constexpr, KD: tl.constexpr, VD: tl.constexpr,
+    BT: tl.constexpr, NT: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    bh = tl.program_id(0)
+    nt = tl.program_id(1)
+    b = bh // H
+    h = bh % H
+    nidx = bh * NT + nt
+
+    row = tl.arange(0, BT)
+    col = tl.arange(0, BT)
+
+    # ---- load this chunk's q,k,v,g (B,T,H,D contiguous) ----
+    p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(QP + (b * T + 0) * (H * KD) + h * KD, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1),
+                            (nt * BT, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_k = tl.make_block_ptr(KP + (b * T + 0) * (H * KD) + h * KD, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1),
+                            (nt * BT, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(VP + (b * T + 0) * (H * VD) + h * VD, (T, VD), (H * VD, 1),
+                            (nt * BT, 0), (BT, VD), (1, 0))
+    p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(GP + (b * T + 0) * (H * KD) + h * KD, (T, KD), (H * KD, 1),
+                            (nt * BT, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_be = tl.make_block_ptr(BETAP + b * T * H + h, (T,), (H,), (nt * BT,), (BT,), (0,))
+
+    bq = tl.load(p_q, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32) * scale
+    bk = tl.load(p_k, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    bv = tl.load(p_v, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    bg = tl.load(p_g, boundary_check=(0, 1)).to(tl.float32)
+    bbe = tl.load(p_be, boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32)
+
+    bg = tl.cumsum(bg, axis=0)            # [BT, KD]
+    gexp = tl.exp(bg)
+    gneg = tl.exp(-bg)
+
+    kge = bk * gexp                        # [BT, KD]
+    kgn = bk * gneg                        # [BT, KD]
+
+    # Akk_raw = kge @ kgn^T   [BT, BT]
+    akk_raw = tl.dot(kge, tl.trans(kgn))
+
+    # M = strict-lower of -beta[c] * akk_raw
+    M = tl.where(row[:, None] > col[None, :],
+                 -bbe[:, None] * akk_raw,
+                 tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32))
+
+    # path-sum: A = (I-M)^{-1} - I  via forward substitution (matches reference)
+    A = M
+    for i in range(1, BT):
+        sel = (row == i).to(tl.float32)             # [BT]
+        a_row = tl.sum(A * sel[:, None], axis=0)    # row i
+        upd = tl.sum(a_row[None, :] * A, axis=0)    # a_row @ A
+        mask = sel[:, None] & (col[None, :] < i)
+        A = tl.where(mask, A + upd[None, :], A)
+    A = A + (row[:, None] == col[None, :]).to(tl.float32)   # + I
+    A = A * bbe[None, :]                                     # diag(beta_j) columns
+
+    w = tl.dot(A, kge)                                  # A @ (exp(g) k)
+    u = tl.dot(A, bv)                                   # A @ v
+    qg = bq * gexp                                      # q*exp(g)
+    aqq = tl.dot(qg, tl.trans(kgn))                     # (q*exp(g)) @ (k*exp(-g))^T
+    aqq = tl.where(row[:, None] >= col[None, :], aqq, tl.zeros([BT, BT], dtype=tl.float32))
+
+    g_last = tl.sum(bg * (row == (BT - 1)).to(tl.float32)[:, None], axis=0)  # [KD]
+    gle = tl.exp(g_last)                                # [KD]
+    dec = tl.exp(g_last[None, :] - bg) * bk             # [BT, KD]
+
+    # ---- store ----
+    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(UP + nidx * BT * VD, (BT, VD), (VD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, VD), (1, 0))
+    p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_dec = tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+    p_aqq = tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP + nidx * BT * BT, (BT, BT), (BT, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_u, u.to(p_u.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(p_w, w.to(p_w.dtype.eleme

... (5751 more chars)

     tl.store(p_aqq, aqq.to(p_aqq.dtype.element_ty))
     # gle [KD]
     tl.store(GLEP + nidx * KD + tl.arange(0, KD), gle)

+
+# ============================================================================
+# Inter-chunk recurrence kernel
+# ============================================================================
+@triton.autotune(
+    configs=[
+        triton.Config({"BV": 64}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
+        triton.Config({"BV": 64}, num_warps=8, num_stages=2),
+        triton.Config({"BV": 32}, num_warps=4, num_stages=2),
+        triton.Config({"BV": 32}, num_warps=2, num_stages=2),
+        triton.Config({"BV": 128}, num_warps=8, num_stages=2),
+        triton.Config({"BV": 16}, num_warps=2, num_stages=2),
+    ],
+    key=["H", "NT"],
+)
+@triton.jit
+def _kda_inter_kernel(
+    UP, WP, QGP, AQQP, DECP, GLEP,
+    OP,
+    T,
+    H: tl.constexpr, KD: tl.constexpr, VD: tl.constexpr,
+    BT: tl.constexpr, NT: tl.constexpr,
+    BV: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    bh = tl.program_id(0)
+    nv = tl.program_id(1)
+    b = bh // H
+    h = bh % H
+    voff = nv * BV
+
+    S = tl.zeros([KD, BV], dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for i in range(NT):
+        nidx = bh * NT + i
+        p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(WP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+        p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(QGP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+        p_dec = tl.make_block_ptr(DECP + nidx * BT * KD, (BT, KD), (KD, 1), (0, 0), (BT, KD), (1, 0))
+        p_aqq = tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP + nidx * BT * BT, (BT, BT), (BT, 1), (0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+        p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(UP + nidx * BT * VD, (BT, VD), (VD, 1), (0, voff), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
+        w = tl.load(p_w)
+        qg = tl.load(p_qg)
+        dec = tl.load(p_dec)
+        aqq = tl.load(p_aqq)
+        u = tl.load(p_u)
+        gle = tl.load(GLEP + nidx * KD + tl.arange(0, KD))   # [KD]
+
+        v_i = u - tl.dot(w, S)                       # [BT, BV]
+        o_i = tl.dot(qg, S) + tl.dot(aqq, v_i)       # [BT, BV]
+        S = S * gle[:, None]
+        S = tl.dot(tl.trans(dec), v_i, S)            # S += dec^T @ v_i
+
+        p_o = tl.make_block_ptr(OP + b * T * H * VD + h * VD + voff, (T, VD), (H * VD, 1),
+                                (i * BT, 0), (BT, BV), (1, 0))
+        tl.store(p_o, o_i.to(OP.dtype.element_ty))

"""Numeric distribution stress cases for correctness checks.

These cases are not hidden shapes. They rerun the same shape/seed validation
under a few scale regimes that catch kernels that only work for the nominal
N(0, 1)-ish inputs.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import os
from collections.abc import Iterator, Mapping, Sequence
from contextlib import contextmanager
from dataclasses import dataclass, field

import torch

ToleranceOverride = Mapping[str, float | Mapping[str, float]]


@dataclass(frozen=True)
class NumericStressCase:
    name: str
    input_scales: Mapping[int, float] = field(default_factory=dict)
    state_scales: Mapping[str, float] = field(default_factory=dict)
    tolerance: ToleranceOverride | None = None


NOMINAL_CASE = NumericStressCase("nominal")

_SMALL_BF16 = {"bfloat16": {"atol": 1e-4, "rtol": 5e-2}}
_MED_BF16 = {"bfloat16": {"atol": 5e-4, "rtol": 5e-2}}
_LARGE_BF16 = {"bfloat16": {"atol": 2e-1, "rtol": 5e-2}}
_TINY_FP32 = {"float32": {"atol": 1e-7, "rtol": 1e-4}}
_LARGE_FP32 = {"float32": {"atol": 1e-1, "rtol": 1e-4}}

_CASES: dict[str, tuple[NumericStressCase, ...]] = {
    "01_fp8_gemm": (
        # fp8 x fp8 has accumulation-order noise vs the bf16-matmul reference that
        # scales with input magnitude; atols are calibrated to absorb it (measured
        # fp8-MMA residual x ~1.5 margin) while rtol=5e-2 still catches gross error.
        NumericStressCase("small_input", input_scales={0: 1e-3},
                          tolerance={

BV=16: S[128,16]=8KB, w[64,128]=32KB, qg=32KB, dec=32KB, aqq[64,64]=16KB → 120KB. Still over! Even BV=16. Because the 3 K-tiles dominate (96KB) + aqq 16KB = 112KB > 101KB. So the K-tiles (w,qg,dec each 32KB fp32) are the problem regardless of BV. I MUST reduce those. Options: (a) bf16 storage (16KB each): 48+8(aqq bf16)+S = fits. Actually, let me reconsider — maybe even simpler: the dots in inter, can I make the reference-matching work with TF32 instead of ieee, by making the INTRA fully ieee-accurate so A is exact, then the recurrence TF32 error is bounded? The issue: under large_qkv, |A| is huge. w=A@kge, |w| huge. w@S huge. TF32 error ~0.004 relative → absolute error 0.004*|w@S|. If |w@S| ~ 100, error ~0.4. Over atol 0.05 → fail. So TF32 in recurrence fails under large_qkv. Need ieee or bf16... bf16 is worse than tf32. So neither works for the recurrence dots under large_qkv if |w@S| is large. Let me actually measure the reference output magnitude under large_qkv. Hmm, I'm spending a lot of reasoning. Let me just be pragmatic: 1. Keep intra fully ieee (inverse accurate). ✓ already. 2. For inter, use ieee dots BUT solve the smem by bf16-storing the tiles w,qg,dec (NOT u, NOT the math) and... no, ieee dot needs fp32 operands. The contradiction: ieee dots need fp32 tiles in smem (big), but smem is limited. Resolution: Block the K-dim of the DOTS (not the state split). Keep S[128,BV] resident fp32. For w@S where w[64,128]: load w in 2 blocks of [64,64], and for each block load S_block[64,BV], do partial dot, accumulate. But S is resident — I don't load S_block from global, I slice the resident S tile. Can I dot a [64,64] w_block with a [64,BV] slice of resident S? In Triton, if S is a [128,BV] register tile, I can slice it: S_lo = S[:64,:] conceptually via tl.dot(w_blk, S_blk) where S_blk is a view. Triton supports slicing tiles? You can do `tl.dot(w_blk, S[:BK,:])`? Not directly with arbitrary slicing, but I can keep S as two separate tiles S0[64,BV] and S1[64,BV], and load w0[64,64], w1[64,64] blocks. Then w@S = dot(w0,S0) + dot(w1,S1). Each dot is [64,64]@[64,BV]. Smem per dot: w_blk[64,64]=16KB, S_blk[64,BV]. With BV=32: S_blk[64,32]=8KB. So each partial dot ~24KB smem, sequential. Peak smem ~ one dot at a time + resident S(16KB) + other tiles. Much better! This requires splitting the KD=128 into 2 blocks of 64 for w,qg,dec,gle, and S into S0[64,BV]+S1[64,BV]. This blocks everything to [64,64] tiles → small smem. And keeps ieee precision. This is more code but solves smem + keeps ieee. Let me implement it. BK=64 constexpr, NBK=KD//BK=2. Store intermediates as fp32 still (for precision), but load in [BT,BK]=[64,64] blocks. w stored as (N, BT, KD). Peak: maybe 2-3 tiles ~48KB. Should fit. Let me implement and the autotune can pick BV. But this doubles the number of dot calls (8 dots per chunk vs 4). More instruction issue but each smaller. Wait, there's a concern: Triton's `S = [tl.zeros(...) for _ in range(NK)]` — can I use a Python list of tiles and index with `S[kb]` where kb is a runtime/loop var? The outer `for kb in range(NK)` is a python-level loop (NK is constexpr=2), so it unrolls. But indexing a Python list inside the kernel with a constexpr index — should work since NK is constexpr and the loop unrolls at compile time. Actually, Triton supports static python loops. `S[kb]` with kb constexpr index into a python list of tensors — Triton's frontend should handle this (it's metaprogramming). Let me test. Actually, there's risk Triton doesn't like a list of tensors updated in place. `S[kb] = ...` reassigns list element. Since unrolled, each becomes a distinct variable. Should be OK. Let me test.

+"""Diagnose large_qkv divergence."""
+import torch
+import reference, solution
+
+B, T, H, K, V, CS = 2, 1024, 8, 128, 128, 64
+for mod in (reference, solution):
+    for k_name in ("B","T","H","K","V","CHUNK_SIZE"):
+        setattr(mod, k_name, locals()[k_name])
+dev = torch.device("cuda:0")
+torch.manual_seed(42)
+q, k, v, g, beta = [t.to(dev) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
+# large_qkv: scale q,k,v by 2
+q, k, v = q*2, k*2, v*2
+ref_m = reference.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(dev).eval()
+sol_m = solution.Model(*solution.get_init_inputs()).to(dev).eval()
+with torch.no_grad():
+    ro = ref_m(q, k, v, g, beta)
+    so = sol_m(q, k, v, g, beta)
+print("ref o absmax", ro.float().abs().max().item())
+print("sol o absmax", so.float().abs().max().item())
+print("max abs diff", (ro.float()-so.float()).abs().max().item())
+
+# Inspect the inverse magnitude for one (b,h) chunk via reference internals
+# Rebuild the intra A matrix the way reference does, fp32.
+import einops
+from einops import rearrange
+bt = CS
+NT = T // bt
+qf = q.float()*ref_m.scale; kf=k.float(); vf=v.float(); gf=g.float(); bef=beta.float()
+qf = qf.view(B,NT,bt,H,K).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous()
+kf = kf.view(B,NT,bt,H,K).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous()
+gf = gf.view(B,NT,bt,H,K).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous()
+bef = bef.view(B,NT,bt,H).permute(0,3,1,2).contiguous()
+gf = gf.cumsum(-2)
+mask = torch.triu(torch.ones(bt,bt,dtype=torch.bool,device=dev),0)
+A = torch.zeros(*qf.shape[:-1],bt,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
+for i in range(bt):
+    k_i = kf[...,i,:]; g_i=gf[...,i:i+1,:]
+    A[...,i] = torch.einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", kf*(gf-g_i).exp(), k_i)
+A = A*bef[...,None]
+A = -A.masked_fill(mask,0)
+M = A.clone()
+for i in range(1,bt):
+    A[...,i,:i]=A[...,i,:i].clone()+(A[...,i,:,None].clone()*A[...,:,:i].clone()).sum(-2)
+A=(A+torch.eye(bt,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev))*bef[...,None,:]
+print("M absmax", M.abs().max().item())
+print("A(inv) absmax", A.abs().max().item())
+# condition: how big do inverse entries get
+print("A[in chunk0] row stats: max", A[0,0,0].abs().max().item(), "mean", A[0,0,0].abs().mean().item())

+"""Isolate: my Triton intra outputs vs PyTorch reference intra, under large_qkv."""
+import torch
+import solution
+
+B, T, H, K, V, CS = 2, 1024, 8, 128, 128, 64
+dev = torch.device("cuda:0")
+torch.manual_seed(42)
+q = torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+k = torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+v = torch.randn(B,T,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+g = (torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)*0.1-0.05)
+beta = torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev))
+scale = K**-0.5
+
+# PyTorch reference intra (from the passing baseline math)
+def intra_torch(q,k,v,g,beta,scale,BT=64):
+    B,T,H,K = q.shape; V=v.shape[-1]; NT=T//BT
+    q=q.float()*scale; k=k.float(); v=v.float(); g=g.float(); beta=beta.float()
+    ch=lambda x: x.view(B,NT,BT,H,-1).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous()
+    q,k,v,g=ch(q),ch(k),ch(v),ch(g)
+    beta=beta.view(B,NT,BT,H).permute(0,3,1,2).contiguous()
+    g=g.cumsum(-2); gexp=g.exp(); gneg=(-g).exp()
+    kg=k*gexp; kgn=k*gneg
+    Akk=torch.matmul(kg,kgn.transpose(-1,-2))
+    idx=torch.arange(BT,device=dev); sl=idx[:,None]>idx[None,:]; eye=torch.eye(BT,device=dev)
+    M=torch.where(sl,-beta[...,None]*Akk,torch.zeros((),device=dev))
+    Tinv=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(eye-M,eye.expand_as(eye-M).contiguous(),upper=False,unitriangular=True)
+    A=Tinv*beta[...,None,:]
+    w=torch.matmul(A,gexp*k); u=torch.matmul(A,v)
+    Aqk=torch.matmul(q*gexp,kgn.transpose(-1,-2))
+    causal=idx[:,None]>=idx[None,:]; Aqk=torch.where(causal,Aqk,torch.zeros((),device=dev))
+    return w,u,Aqk,A
+
+wt,ut,Aqt,At = intra_torch(q,k,v,g,beta,scale)
+# my triton intra
+U,W,QG,AQQ,DEC,GLE,B,H,NT,KD,VD = solution._kda_intra(q,k,v,g,beta,scale,CS)
+def bh(t): return t.view(B,H,NT,CS,-1)
+Wm=bh(W); Um=bh(U); AQQm=AQQ.view(B,H,NT,CS,CS)
+print("w  max diff", (wt-Wm.float()).abs().max().item(), "ref absmax", wt.abs().max().item())
+print("u  max diff", (ut-Um.float()).abs().max().item(), "ref absmax", ut.abs().max().item())
+print("Aqk max diff", (Aqt-AQQm.float()).abs().max().item(), "ref absmax", Aqt.abs().max().item())

+"""Compare my path-sum loop (in pytorch) vs solve_triangular, under large_qkv."""
+import torch
+dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
+B,T,H,K=2,1024,8,128; BT=64; NT=T//BT
+torch.manual_seed(42)
+k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)*0.1-0.05)
+beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev))
+kf=k.float().view(B,NT,BT,H,K).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous()
+gf=g.float().view(B,NT,BT,H,K).permute(0,3,1,2,4).contiguous().cumsum(-2)

+akk=(kge@kgn.T)  # [BT,BT]

+# reference A via solve_triangular
+sl=idx[:,None]>idx[None,:]; eye=torch.eye(BT,device=dev)
+M=torch.where(sl,-b[:,None]*akk,torch.zeros((),device=dev))
+A_solve=torch.linalg.solve_triangular(eye-M,eye,upper=False,unitriangular=True)*b[None,:]

+    A=torch.where(mask,A+upd[None,:],A)
+A=A+torch.eye(BT,device=dev)
+A=A*b[None,:]
+print("pathsum vs solve max diff:", (A-A_solve).abs().max().item())

+"""Run reference.py's VERBATIM intra loop on a single (b,h) and compare orders."""
+import torch
+from einops import rearrange
+dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
+B,T,H,K=2,1024,8,128; BT=64; NT=T//BT
+torch.manual_seed(42)
+k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)*0.1-0.05)
+beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev))
+# reference verbatim (full batched)
+kf=rearrange(k.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
+gf=rearrange(g.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
+bef=rearrange(beta.float(),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
+mask=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=dev),0)
+A=torch.zeros(*kf.shape[:-1],BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
+for i in range(BT):
+    k_i=kf[...,i,:]; g_i=gf[...,i:i+1,:]
+    A[...,i]=torch.einsum('... c d, ... d -> ... c', kf*(gf-g_i).exp(), k_i)
+A=A*bef[...,None]
+A=-A.masked_fill(mask,0)
+Aref_loop=A.clone()
+for i in range(1,BT):
+    Aref_loop[...,i,:i]=Aref_loop[...,i,:i].clone()+(Aref_loop[...,i,:,None].clone()*Aref_loop[...,:,:i].clone()).sum(-2)
+Aref_loop=(Aref_loop+torch.eye(BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev))*bef[...,None,:]
+print("reference verbatim loop A[0,0,0] absmax:", Aref_loop[0,0,0].abs().max().item())
+
+# Now: does reference.py's actual Model output match path-sum-A or solve-A?
+import reference
+reference.B=B;reference.T=T;reference.H=H;reference.K=K;reference.V=K;reference.CHUNK_SIZE=BT
+q=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+v=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+m=reference.Model(B,T,H,K,K,BT).to(dev).eval()
+with torch.no_grad(): o_ref=m(q,k,v,g,beta)
+print("reference.py o absmax:", o_ref.float().abs().max().item())
+print("reference.py o[0,0,0] sample:", o_ref[0,0,0,:4].float().tolist())

It should be `a_row[:, None]`. This is the bug! Let me fix it in the Triton kernel: `upd = tl.sum(a_row[:, None] * A, axis=0)`. That explains why nominal "mostly worked" (12% error) — the wrong formula happened to be approximately OK for small M (where the inverse ≈ I + M and the error is second-order), but diverges for larger M. Let me fix it.
in 0out 0cache_r 0cache_w 0
assistant
Found the bug! In the path-sum loop, `upd = tl.sum(a_row[None, :] * A, axis=0)` broadcasts `a_row` over the wrong axis — it computes `a_row[j]*sum_m A[m,j]` instead of `sum_m a_row[m]*A[m,j]`. It must be `a_row[:, None]`. This is wrong in both my PyTorch replication and the Triton kernel, which is why nominal "mostly worked" (≈OK for small M) but diverged under large_qkv.

+"""Profile per-kernel time."""
+import torch
+import solution
+from torch.profiler import profile, ProfilerActivity
+
+B,T,H,K,V,CS=2,2048,8,128,128,64
+for mod in (solution,):
+    mod.B=B;mod.T=T;mod.H=H;mod.K=K;mod.V=V;mod.CHUNK_SIZE=CS
+dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
+torch.manual_seed(0)
+q,k,v,g,beta=[t.to(dev) for t in solution.get_inputs()]
+m=solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(dev).eval()
+with torch.no_grad():
+    for _ in range(3): m(q,k,v,g,beta)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    # time each stage
+    import time
+    for label, fn in [("full", lambda: m(q,k,v,g,beta)),
+                      ("intra", lambda: solution._kda_intra(q,k,v,g,beta,m.scale,CS))]:
+        for _ in range(5): fn()
+        torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        t0=time.time()
+        for _ in range(50): fn()
+        torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        print(f"{label}: {(time.time()-t0)/50*1000:.3f} ms")

+"""Which inverse methods reproduce reference.py under large_qkv?"""
+import torch
+from einops import rearrange
+dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
+B,T,H,K,BT=2,1024,8,128,64; NT=T//BT; V=K
+torch.manual_seed(42)
+q=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+v=torch.randn(B,T,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
+g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)*0.1-0.05)
+beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev))
+scale=K**-0.5
+
+def make_M():
+    kf=rearrange(k.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
+    gf=rearrange(g.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
+    bef=rearrange(beta.float(),'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
+    gexp=gf.exp(); kgn=(-gf).exp(); kge=kf*gexp
+    akk=torch.matmul(kge,kgn.transpose(-1,-2))
+    idx=torch.arange(BT,device=dev); sl=idx[:,None]>idx[None,:]
+    M=torch.where(sl,-bef[...,None]*akk,torch.zeros((),device=dev))
+    return M,bef,gexp,kgn,kf,kge
+
+M,bef,gexp,kgn,kf,kge=make_M()
+eye=torch.eye(BT,device=dev)
+# method 1: path-sum (reference exact)
+def pathsum(M):
+    A=M.clone()
+    idx=torch.arange(BT,device=dev)
+    for i in range(1,BT):
+        A[...,i,:i]=A[...,i,:i].clone()+(A[...,i,:,None].clone()*A[...,:,:i].clone()).sum(-2)
+    return (A+eye)
+# method 2: solve_triangular
+def solve(M):
+    return torch.linalg.solve_triangular(eye-M,eye.expand(*M.shape).contiguous(),upper=False,unitriangular=True)
+# method 3: doubling  (I-M)^{-1}=sum M^k via S,P doubling
+def doubling(M):
+    S=torch.eye(BT,device=dev).expand(*M.shape).contiguous()
+    P=M.clone()
+    for _ in range(6):  # 1,2,4,...,64
+        S=S+P@S
+        P=P@P
+    return S
+
+def run_with_Ainv(Ainv_noeye):  # Ainv_noeye = (I-M)^{-1} (without final beta col)
+    A=Ainv_noeye*bef[...,None,:]
+    w=torch.matmul(A,gexp*kf); u=torch.matmul(A,v.float().view(B,NT,BT,H,V).permute(0,3,1,2,4))
+    # full recurrence
+    qf=rearrange(q.float()*scale,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
+    vf=rearrange(v.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
+    gf=rearrange(g.float(),'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT).cumsum(-2)
+    aqq=torch.matmul(qf*gexp,kgn.transpose(-1,-2))
+    idx=torch.arange(BT,device=dev); causal=idx[:,None]>=idx[None,:]
+    aqq=torch.where(causal,aqq,torch.zeros((),device=dev))
+    qg=qf*gexp
+    S=torch.zeros(B,H,K,V,device=dev)
+    o=torch.zeros(B,H,NT,BT,V,device=dev)
+    gle=gf[...,-1,:].exp(); dec=(gf[...,-1:,:]-gf).exp()*kf
+    for i in range(NT):
+        v_i=u[:,:,i]-torch.matmul(w[:,:,i],S)
+        o[:,:,i]=torch.matmul(qg[:,:,i],S)+torch.matmul(aqq[:,:,i],v_i)
+        S=S*gle[:,:,i,:,None]
+        S=S+torch.matmul(dec[:,:,i].transpose(-1,-2),v_i)
+    return rearrange(o,'b h n c d -> b (n c) h d')
+
+import reference
+reference.B=B;reference.T=T;reference.H=H;reference.K=K;reference.V=V;reference.CHUNK_SIZE=BT
+m=reference.Model(B,T,H,K,V,BT).to(dev).eval()
+with torch.no_grad(): o_ref=m(q,k,v,g,beta).float()
+print("ref o absmax", o_ref.abs().max().item())
+for name,fn in [("pathsum",pathsum),("solve",solve),("doubling",doubling)]:
+    Ainv=fn(M)
+    o=run_with_Ainv(Ainv)
+    print(f"{name}: max_abs_diff vs ref = {(o-o_ref).abs().max().item():.5f}")

import torch
from einops import rearrange
import reference
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
B,T,H,K,BT=2,1024,8,128,64; NT=T//BT; V=K
reference.B=B;reference.T=T;reference.H=H;reference.K=K;reference.V=V;reference.CHUNK_SIZE=BT
torch.manual_seed(42)

k=torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
v=torch.randn(B,T,H,V,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev)*0.1*2
g=(torch.randn(B,T,H,K,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)*0.1-0.05)
beta=torch.sigmoid(torch.randn(B,T,H,dtype=torch.bfloat16,device=dev))

# Copy reference's EXACT internal computation, capturing A
src=reference._naive_chunk_kda.__code__
# just call a hand-copy of the relevant part
dtype=v.dtype; scale=K**-0.5
qf,kf,vf,gf,bef=[x.to(torch.float32) for x in (q*scale,k,v,g,beta)]
qf=rearrange(qf,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
kf=rearrange(kf,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
vf=rearrange(vf,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
gf=rearrange(gf,'b (n c) h d -> b h n c d',c=BT)
bef=rearrange(bef,'b (n c) h -> b h n c',c=BT)
gf=gf.cumsum(-2)
mask=torch.triu(torch.ones(BT,BT,dtype=torch.bool,device=dev),0)
A=torch.zeros(*qf.shape[:-1],BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
for i in range(BT):
    k_i=kf[...,i,:]; g_i=gf[...,i:i+1,:]
    A[...,i]=torch.einsum('... c d, ... d -> ... c', kf*(gf-g_i).exp(), k_i)
A=A*bef[...,None]
A=-A.masked_fill(mask,0)
for i in range(1,BT):
    A[...,i,:i]=A[...,i,:i].clone()+(A[...,i,:,None].clone()*A[...,:,:i].clone()).sum(-2)
A=(A+torch.eye(BT,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev))*bef[...,None,:]
print("ref A absmax", A.abs().max().item())
w=torch.matmul(A,gf.exp()*kf)
u=torch.matmul(A,vf)
print("w absmax", w.abs().max().item())
print("u absmax", u.abs().max().item())
m=reference.Model(B,T,H,K,V,BT).to(dev).eval()
with torch.no_grad(): o=m(q,k,v,g,beta)
print("o absmax", o.float().abs().max().item())

-    A = A + (row[:, None] == col[None, :]).to(tl.float32)   # + I
-    A = A * bbe[None, :]                                     # diag(beta_j) columns
+    # (I - M)^{-1} = sum_{k=0}^{BT-1} M^k  (M is strict-lower, nilpotent of
+    # degree BT). Computed by S,P doubling (6 doublings for BT=64) using
+    # tensor-core matmuls instead of a 63-step serial forward substitution.
+    # The KDA output is numerically robust to the inverse (delta structure),
+    # so this matches the reference within tolerance.
+    I = (row[:, None] == col[None, :]).to(tl.float32)
+    S = I
+    P = M
+    for _ in range(6):                  # n: 1 -> 64
+        S = S + tl.dot(P, S)
+        P = tl.dot(P, P)
+    A = S * bbe[None, :]                # diag(beta_j) columns
 
     w = tl.dot(A, kge)                                  # A @ (exp(g) k)
     u = tl.dot(A, bv)                                   # A @ v

import torch, reference, solution, os
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
n=os.environ["KBH_NSTEPS"]
worst=0
for B,T,H,K,V,CS in [(2,1024,8,128,128,64),(2,2048,8,128,128,64),(1,4096,8,128,128,64),(1,2048,4,128,128,64)]:

    for seed in (42,123,456):
        for sq in (1.0,2.0):
            torch.manual_seed(seed)
            q,k,v,g,beta=[t.to(dev) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
            q,k,v=q*sq,k*sq,v*sq
            rm=reference.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(dev).eval(); sm=solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(dev).eval()
            with torch.no_grad(): d=(rm(q,k,v,g,beta).float()-sm(q,k,v,g,beta).float()).abs().max().item()
            worst=max(worst,d)
print(f"n=$n worst_largeqkv_diff={worst:.5f}")
EOF

python - <<'EOF' 2>&1 | grep -iE "intra|register|shared|occupancy|warps|best"
import torch, solution
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
B,T,H,K,V,CS=2,2048,8,128,128,64
solution.B=B;solution.T=T;solution.H=H;solution.K=K;solution.V=V;solution.CHUNK_SIZE=CS
torch.manual_seed(0)
q,k,v,g,beta=[t.to(dev) for t in solution.get_inputs()]
# trigger compile + autotune
U,W,QG,AQQ,DEC,GLE,*_=solution._kda_intra(q,k,v,g,beta,K**-0.5,CS)
kern=solution._kda_intra_kernel
for cfg in kern.cache:
    kk=kern.cache[cfg]
    print("intra cfg", cfg, "regs/smem/occ?")
    # metadata
    try:
        m=kk.metadata
        print("  num_warps",m.num_warps,"num_stages",m.num_stages,"shared",getattr(m,'shared',None))
    except Exception as e:
        print("  meta err",e)
    break

import torch, solution
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
B,T,H,K,V,CS=2,2048,8,128,128,64
solution.B=B;solution.T=T;solution.H=H;solution.K=K;solution.V=V;solution.CHUNK_SIZE=CS
torch.manual_seed(0)

print("intra best:", solution._kda_intra_kernel.best_config)
o=torch.empty(B,T,H,V,device=dev,dtype=torch.bfloat16)
solution._kda_inter_kernel[(16,2)](U,W,QG,AQQ,DEC,GLE,o,T,H=8,KD=128,VD=128,BT=64,NT=32)
print("inter best:", solution._kda_inter_kernel.best_config)

In Triton, extracting row BT-1 from [BT,BK]: glast = sum(gcs * (row==BT-1)[:,None], axis=0) → [BK]. - gle_block = exp(glast); store gle - dec_block = exp(glast[None,:]-gcs)*k; store dec After loop: aqq causal-masked, store. u = A@v: separate small loop over V-blocks (or BV=full 128 in one dot if registers allow — A[64,64]@v[64,128], v[64,128] is one tile... that's the register hog again). Block u over V too: BVK=32. This is a lot but let me write it. Actually, u and w have the SAME structure (A @ something[64,128]). Let me handle both K-dim (w, dec, gle, aqq) and V-dim (u) blocks. Hmm, u is A@v where v is [64,VD=128]. Block over V: BVK=32, NV=4. For each vb: load v[64,BVK]; u_block=A@v; store. Let me write this. It's verbose but should eliminate spilling. Actually, this is getting really long. Let me reconsider if there's a more surgical fix. The spilling is REG:255 + STACK. The biggest contributors to register pressure are the [64,128] tiles. The inverse 64×64 tiles (M,A,S,P) are also big but fewer. Quick alternative: maybe just the doubling's S and P cause extra pressure. The doubling currently: S=I, P=M, loop{S=S+P@S; P=P@P}. After loop A=S*beta. During the loop, S and P [64,64] live. Plus M (input to P init, can free after). Plus akk_raw (freed after M). So during doubling: S, P [64,64] = 8K = 64 regs. Not the main issue. The main issue: kge, kgn [64,128] held for akk AND later w/aqq. Plus bq, bk, bv, bg. Let me just do the K-blocking. It's the right fix. Let me write it. Let me write the K-blocked intra kernel. I'll keep it as clean as possible. Actually, let me reconsider time. This is a big rewrite with correctness risk. Let me do it incrementally and test. Let me write it. Let me define BK=32. The kernel: ```python @triton.jit def _kda_intra_kernel(QP,KP,VP,GP,BETAP, UP,WP,QGP,AQQP,DECP,GLEP, scale, T, H:tl.constexpr, KD:tl.constexpr, VD:tl.constexpr, BT:tl.constexpr, NT:tl.constexpr, BK:tl.constexpr, BVK:tl.constexpr, NSTEPS:tl.constexpr): bh=tl.program_id(0); nt=tl.program_id(1) b=bh//H; h=bh%H; nidx=bh*NT+nt row=tl.arange(0,BT); col=tl.arange(0,BT) NK: tl.constexpr = KD//BK NVK: tl.constexpr = VD//BVK # beta p_be=tl.make_block_ptr(BETAP+b*T*H+h,(T,),(H,),(nt*BT,),(BT,),(0,)) bbe=tl.load(p_be,boundary_check=(0,)).to(tl.float32) # ---- Pass A: akk_raw ---- akk=tl.zeros([BT,BT],dtype=tl.float32) for kb in range(NK): off=kb*BK p_g=tl.make_block_ptr(GP+(b*T)*(H*KD)+h*KD,(T,KD),(H*KD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) p_k=tl.make_block_ptr(KP+(b*T)*(H*KD)+h*KD,(T,KD),(H*KD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) gcs=tl.cumsum(tl.load(p_g,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32),axis=0) k=tl.load(p_k,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32) kge=k*tl.exp(gcs); kgn=k*tl.exp(-gcs) akk += tl.dot(kge, tl.trans(kgn)) M=tl.where(row[:,None]>col[None,:], -bbe[:,None]*akk, tl.zeros([BT,BT],dtype=tl.float32)) # inverse via doubling I=(row[:,None]==col[None,:]).to(tl.float32) S=I; P=M for _ in range(NSTEPS): S=S+tl.dot(P,S); P=tl.dot(P,P) A=S*bbe[None,:] # column beta # ---- Pass B: w, aqq, dec, gle (K-blocks); u (V-blocks) ---- lastidx=(row==(BT-1)).to(tl.float32) aqq=tl.zeros([BT,BT],dtype=tl.float32) for kb in range(NK): off=kb*BK p_g=tl.make_block_ptr(GP+(b*T)*(H*KD)+h*KD,(T,KD),(H*KD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) p_k=tl.make_block_ptr(KP+(b*T)*(H*KD)+h*KD,(T,KD),(H*KD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) p_q=tl.make_block_ptr(QP+(b*T)*(H*KD)+h*KD,(T,KD),(H*KD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) gcs=tl.cumsum(tl.load(p_g,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32),axis=0) k=tl.load(p_k,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32); q=tl.load(p_q,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32)*scale gexp=tl.exp(gcs); gneg=tl.exp(-gcs) kge=k*gexp; kgn=k*gneg wblk=tl.dot(A,kge) # [BT,BK] p_w=tl.make_block_ptr(WP+nidx*BT*KD,(BT,KD),(KD,1),(0,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) tl.store(p_w, wblk.to(p_w.dtype.element_ty)) aqq += tl.dot(q*gexp, tl.trans(kgn)) glast=tl.sum(gcs*lastidx[:,None],axis=0) # [BK] gle=tl.exp(glast) dec=tl.exp(glast[None,:]-gcs)*k # [BT,BK] p_dec=tl.make_block_ptr(DECP+nidx*BT*KD,(BT,KD),(KD,1),(0,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) tl.store(p_dec, dec.to(p_dec.dtype.element_ty)) p_qg=tl.make_block_ptr(QGP+nidx*BT*KD,(BT,KD),(KD,1),(0,off),(BT,BK),(1,0)) tl.store(p_qg, (q*gexp).to(p_qg.dtype.element_ty)) tl.store(GLEP+nidx*KD+off+tl.arange(0,BK), gle) aqq=tl.where(row[:,None]>=col[None,:],aqq,tl.zeros([BT,BT],dtype=tl.float32)) p_aqq=tl.make_block_ptr(AQQP+nidx*BT*BT,(BT,BT),(BT,1),(0,0),(BT,BT),(1,0)) tl.store(p_aqq, aqq.to(p_aqq.dtype.element_ty)) # u over V-blocks for vb in range(NVK): off=vb*BVK p_v=tl.make_block_ptr(VP+(b*T)*(H*VD)+h*VD,(T,VD),(H*VD,1),(nt*BT,off),(BT,BVK),(1,0)) v=tl.load(p_v,boundary_check=(0,1)).to(tl.float32) ublk=tl.dot(A,v) p_u=tl.make_block_ptr(UP+nidx*BT*VD,(BT,VD),(VD,1),(0,off),(BT,BVK),(1,0)) tl.store(p_u, ublk.to(p_u.dtype.element_ty)) ``` This K-blocks everything, keeping tiles at [BT,BK]=[64,32]. Should drastically reduce registers. Note: qg is needed by inter. In the current design, inter uses qg=qg_i for qg@S. I store qg. Good. (qg = q*gexp = q_scaled * gexp.) import torch, solution, time
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
for B,T,H,K,V,CS in [(2,2048,8,128,128,64),(1,2048,4,128,128,64),(1,4096,8,128,128,64)]:
    solution.B=B;solution.T=T;solution.H=H;solution.K=K;solution.V=V;solution.CHUNK_SIZE=CS
    torch.manual_seed(0)
    q,k,v,g,beta=[t.to(dev) for t in solution.get_inputs()]
    m=solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(dev).eval()
    def t_fn(fn,n=30):
        for _ in range(5): fn()
        torch.cuda.synchronize(); t0=time.time()
        for _ in range(n): fn()
        torch.cuda.synchronize(); return (time.time()-t0)/n*1000
    full=t_fn(lambda:m(q,k,v,g,beta))
    intra=t_fn(lambda:solution._kda_intra(q,k,v,g,beta,m.scale,CS))
    print(f"shape B={B}T={T}H={H}: full={full:.3f} intra={intra:.3f} inter~{full-intra:.3f}")
EOF

python - <<'EOF' 2>&1 | grep -E "BV=|best"
import torch, solution, time
dev=torch.device("cuda:0")
B,T,H,K,V,CS=1,2048,4,128,128,64
solution.B=B;solution.T=T;solution.H=H;solution.K=K;solution.V=V;solution.CHUNK_SIZE=CS
torch.manual_seed(0)
q,k,v,g,beta=[t.to(dev) for t in solution.get_inputs()]
m=solution.Model(B,T,H,K,V,CS).to(dev).eval()
def tm(fn,n=40):
    for _ in range(5): fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize();t0=time.time()
    for _ in range(n):fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize();return(time.time()-t0)/n*1000
print("full default:", tm(lambda:m(q,k,v,g,beta)))
print("inter best config:", solution._kda_inter_kernel.best_config)
# manually sweep BV by clearing cache & forcing
for bv,nw in [(16,2),(16,4),(32,2),(32,4),(64,4),(64,8),(128,8),(8,2),(8,4)]:
    solution._kda_inter_kernel.configs=tuple()
    import triton
    cfg=triton.Config({"BV":bv},num_warps=nw,num_stages=1)
    # bypass autotune: call with explicit config
    U,W,QG,AQQ,DEC,GLE,*_=solution._kda_intra(q,k,v,g,beta,m.scale,CS)
    o=torch.empty(B,T,H,V,device=dev,dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    NV=V//bv
    try:
        for _ in range(3):
            solution._kda_inter_kernel[fn=lambda meta:cfg] if False else None
        # direct launch with config
        sol_kern=solution._kda_inter_kernel
        # simplest: just run and time
        def run():
            o=torch.empty(B,T,H,V,device=dev,dtype=torch.bfloat16)
            sol_kern[(B*H,NV)](U,W,QG,AQQ,DEC,GLE,o,T,H=H,KD=128,VD=128,BT=64,NT=32,BK=64,BV=bv,num_warps=nw,num_stages=1)
        t=tm(run,n=30)
        print(f"BV={bv:3d} nw={nw}: inter={t:.4f}ms")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"BV={bv} nw={nw}: err {type(e).__name__}")

1	"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form. Triton kernels for SM86 (3090).
2	
3	Two-stage chunk-parallel implementation:
4	  - intra kernel:  grid (B*H, NT). Each program builds the per-chunk intra-chunk
5	    transition A = (I-M)^{-1} diag(beta) (M strict-lower), and the local causal
6	    Aqk, plus the decayed quantities consumed by the recurrence. Embarrassingly
7	    parallel over chunks.
8	  - inter kernel:  grid (B*H, NV). Each program owns one V-tile of the recurrent
9	    state S[K,BV] and scans the NT chunks sequentially.
10	
11	Math (matching the FLA chunk-form reference, G=1):
12	  g_cs = cumsum(g) within chunk
13	  Akk_raw[c,j] = sum_d k[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]
14	  M[c,j]       = -beta[c] Akk_raw[c,j]        (strict lower)
15	  A            = (I - M)^{-1} diag(beta_j)
16	  w = A @ (exp(g_cs) k);  u = A @ v
17	  Aqk[c,j]     = sum_d q[c,d] exp(g_cs[c,d]-g_cs[j,d]) k[j,d]   (causal c>=j)
18	  per chunk: v_i = u_i - w_i S;  o_i = (q*exp(g_cs)) S + Aqk v_i
19	             S <- diag(exp(g_cs[last])) S + (exp(g_cs[last]-g_cs) k)^T v_i
20	"""
21	from __future__ import annotations
22	
23	import torch
24	import torch.nn as nn
25	import triton
26	import triton.language as tl
27	
28	OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
29	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
30	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_3090"]

+---
+name: kbhard-kda-on-3090
+description: "KDA cutlass (02): chunk-forward Triton impl on 3090; inverse robustness, K-blocking, ~0.097 peak_fraction"
+metadata:
+  type: project
+---
+
+02_kda_cutlass (Kimi Delta Attention chunk-forward, bf16) now targets RTX_3090
+directly in problem.yaml (peak_tflops bf16 = 71), gate gmean >= 0.1. A clean
+2-kernel Triton impl (intra: per-chunk inverse+w+u+Aqk, grid (B*H,NT); inter:
+sequential chunk recurrence over state S, grid (B*H,NV)) reaches **peak_fraction
+~0.097** (shapes 0/1/2 = B*T=2*1024/2*2048/1*4096 H=8 clear 0.10-0.125; shape3
+B=1 H=4 T=2048 lags at ~0.060 — purely parallelism-limited: B*H=4 with a 32-chunk
+sequential recurrence, can't be fixed without a parallel scan over chunks which
+materializes a [128,128] transition matrix and regresses the strong shapes).
+
+Hard-won technical facts for this problem:
+- The intra-chunk inverse A=(I-M)^{-1} (M strict-lower, =-beta*Akk_raw) is
+  catastrophically ill-conditioned under the large_qkv stress case (q,k,v x2):
+  1-ulp differences in Akk_raw between matmul and einsum reduction orders blow
+  A from ~1 to ~2.7e7. BUT the KDA **output o is numerically robust to A**
+  (delta structure: v_i = A@(v - (g.exp()*k)@S) cancels). So (a) you do NOT
+  need ieee/precise dots — tf32 throughout passes large_qkv at ~1e-3 diff; and
+  (b) you can compute the inverse as a **truncated Neumann series** sum M^0..M^15
+  (S,P doubling, 4 steps) instead of exact path-sum / solve_triangular.
+  nsteps=4 leaves huge margin (~1e-3 worst); nsteps=3 is too risky (~0.048 vs
+  0.05 tol). Reference path-sum loop is `A[i,:i]+=sum_m A[i,m]*A[m,j]` — mind
+  the axis (a_row[:,None] not [None,:]).
+- **K-dimension blocking is the single biggest perf lever** (2x). Loading
+  [BT=64, K=128] fp32 tiles (q,k,v,g,w,qg,dec) blows the reg file on sm86
+  (REG capped 255, STACK spilling, ~6% SM util). Loop K in BK=32/64 blocks,
+  keep tiles at [64,32]; drops regs to ~168, no spill. Same for the inter
+  state S (split into S0,S1 [64,BV]).
+- u and w (=A@v, A@(g.exp()*k)) MUST stay fp32 — they sit in the v_i=u-w@S
+  cancellation. qg, dec, Aqk, gle can be bf16 (cut inter read traffic ~13%).
+- torch default on this box is fp32_matmul_precision=highest, allow_tf32=False
+  (true fp32), so match with tf32 tl.dot (not ieee — ieee blows smem on sm86
+  and is needlessly slow). No ncu (ERR_NVGPUCTRPERM); use cuobjdump -res-usage
+  on TRITON_CACHE_DIR cubins for reg/spill counts.
+- Baseline vectorized-PyTorch (solve_triangular inverse) = 0.0102. Triton
+  naive = 0.029. +Neumann inverse = 0.040. +K-blocking (intra+inter) = 0.083.
+  +bf16 intermed = 0.097. See [[kbhard-run-can-land-on-3090]] for the machine-
+  mismatch context (now resolved: problem targets 3090).

The implementation is complete. Final summary: ## Result: KDA chunk-forward on RTX 3090 (SM86) **`solution.py` — `check.py` PASS, `peak_fraction` ≈ 0.097** (9.5x over the vectorized-PyTorch baseline of 0.0102). Per-shape: B=2/T=1024 → 0.113, B=2/T=2048 → 0.125, B=1/T=4096 → 0.104, B=1/T=2048/H=4 → 0.060. ### What it is A two-kernel Triton implementation (no FLA calls) of the chunk-parallel Kimi Delta Attention forward: - **Intra kernel** (grid `B*H × NT`, embarrassingly parallel over chunks): builds the per-chunk transition `A = (I−M)⁻¹ diag(β)`, plus `w, u, Aqk, decay, qg`. - **Inter kernel** (grid `B*H × NV`): one program per V-tile scans the NT chunks sequentially, carrying the recurrent state `S`. ### The key insights that moved the number 1. **The inverse `(I−M)⁻¹` is ill-conditioned but the *output* is robust to it.** Under the `large_qkv` stress case, `A` swings from ~1 to ~2.7e7 depending on reduction order, yet `o` stays correct because `v_i = A@(v − (eᵍ·k)@S)` cancels. This means: (a) TF32 dots everywhere pass at ~1e-3 diff (no need for slow ieee fp32), and (b) the inverse can be a **truncated Neumann series** `Σ Mᵏ` via S,P-doubling (nsteps=4) instead of the exact 63-step path-sum. → 0.029 → 0.040. 2. **K-dimension blocking is the biggest lever** (0.040 → 0.083). Loading `[64,128]` fp32 tiles blows the sm86 register file (REG capped at 255, heavy spilling, ~6% SM utilization). Looping K in `BK=32/64` blocks drops registers to 168 with zero spill — for both the intra I/O tiles and the inter state `S` (split into `S0,S1`). 3. **bf16 intermediates** for everything except `u` and `w` (which sit in the `v_i = u − w@S` cancellation and must stay fp32). → 0.083 → 0.097. ### The ceiling shape3 (B=1, H=4) is the sole holdout at 0.060 — purely parallelism-limited (B·H=4 with a 32-chunk *sequential* recurrence). Crossing the 0.1 gate cleanly would need a parallel scan over chunks, which materializes a `[128,128]` transition matrix and regresses the three shapes already over 0.1; I judged that not worth the risk to a solid result. The workspace is clean (scratch files removed); the final answer is in `solution.py` only. Memory note `kbhard-kda-on-3090` updated with the findings.
